He first created the waters and deposited in them a seed. This seed became a golden egg, in which he himself was born as Brahmā--the progenitor of all the worlds. Then the Lord divided the egg into two parts, with which he constructed heaven and earth. He then created the ten <lbinfo n='Pra+jāpatis'/> Prajāpatis or mind-born sons who <lbinfo n='complet+ed'/> completed the work of creation. According to another account (Rāmāyaṇa) Brahmā sprang from ether; from him was <lbinfo n='des+cended'/> descended Marīci, and his son was <lbinfo n='Kaśya+pa'/> Kaśyapa. From Kaśyapa sprang Vivasvat, and Manu sprang from him. Thus Manu was the procreator of all human beings. According to a third account, the Supreme deity, after dividing the golden egg, separated himself into two parts, male and female, from which sprang Virāj and from him Manu; <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Ku. 2. 7</ls> and <ls>Ms. 1. 32</ls> <i>et seq.</i>. <lbinfo n='Mytho+logically'/> Mythologically Brahman is represented as <lbinfo n='be+ing'/> being born in a lotus which sprang from the navel of Viṣṇu, and as creating the world by an illicit connection with his own daughter Sarasvatī. Brahman had originally five heads, but one of them was cut down by Śiva with the ring-finger or burnt down by the fire from his third eye. His vehicle is a swan. He has numerous epithets, most of which have reference to his birth in a lotus]. <b>--2</b> A Brāhmaṇa; <ls>Ś. 4. 3.</ls> <b>--3</b> A devout man. <b>--4</b> One of the four R<i>itvijas</i> or priests employed at a Soma sacrifice. <b>--5</b> One conversant with sacred knowledge. <b>--6</b> The sun. <b>--7</b> Intellect. <b>--8</b> An epithet of the seven Prajāpatis: --मरीचि, अत्रि, <lbinfo n='aMgira#s'/> अंगिरस्, पुलस्य, पुलह, क्रतु and वसिष्ठ. <b>--9</b> An epithet of Bṛhaspati. <b>--10</b> Of Śiva. <b>--Comp.</b> --अक्षरं the sacred syllable <i>om</i>. --अंगभूः {1} a horse. {2} one who has touched the several parts of his body by the repetition of <lbinfo n='Man+tras'/> Mantras;             "content": "ब्रह्मन्¦ <i>brahman, a,</i> n. (fr. rt. 2. <i>bṛh</i> = 2. <i>vṛh;</i> cf. rts. <i>vṛṃh, vṛdh</i>), religious devotion (regarded as an impulse or feeling gradually growing up and expanding so as to fill the soul), prayer or any pious expression in the worship of the gods, a hymn of praise (Ved., Sāy. <i>= stotra</i>); a sacred text (especially a Mantra used as a spell for averting evil influences, forming a distinct class from the <i>ṛcas,</i> <i>sāmāni,</i> and <i>yajūṃṣi;</i> and hence the term <i>Brah-</i> <i>ma-veda,</i> q. v., is sometimes applied to the collection of texts commonly called <i>Atharva-veda</i>); the mystic syllable <i>Om</i> [cf. Manu II. 83]; the sacred word or word of God (opposed to <i>vāc,</i> the word of man), the sacred text, the Veda; (in Atharva-veda X. 7, 32, X. 8, 1, there is an allusion to a <i>jyeṣṭham</i> <i>brahma</i> or original pre-æval Veda or Deity? from which the existing Vedas have been drawn); sacred learning, divine science, religious knowledge, theology (speculative or theoretical, as opposed to practical religion, i. e. <i>tapas,</i> &c.); the Brāhmaṇa portion of the Veda [cf. <i>brāhmaṇa</i> and Manu IV. 100]; religious life, celibacy, chastity [cf. <i>brahma-</i> <i>carya,</i> col. 3]; the practice of austerity or penance (<i>=</i> <i>tapas</i>); the Supreme Being regarded as impersonal or in the abstract and divested of all quality and action; the highest object of religious knowledge, the Supreme all-pervading Spirit and Soul of the Universe, the divine essence and source of all being from which all created things emanate and to which they return, the Self-existent, the Absolute, the Eternal (<i>= paramātman, ātman, adhyātma, pra-</i> <i>dhāna, kṣetra-jña, tattva;</i> Brahman as the Supreme Spirit is not an object of worship in the usual sense of the term, but is meditated upon by the devout with profound veneration; he appears in the Atharva-veda as the Supreme Deity, and in X. 7, 24, a highest divine essence or <i>brahma jyeṣṭham</i> is spoken of); <i>= mokṣa,</i> emancipation or liberation from mundane existence; the class occupied with religious knowledge, the Brāhmanical caste as a body, the priestly or sacerdotal class (cf. Manu IX. 322; in one or two passages the neut. <i>brahman</i> appears to = ) a member of the Brāhmanical caste, a Brāhman; (according to the Nirukta) <i>= anna,</i> food; <i>= dhana,</i> wealth; (<i>ā</i>), m. one who prays, a devout man [cf. <i>tuvi-b°</i>]; one whose calling and business consist in praying, a priest, Brāhman [cf. <i>oha-b°</i>]; one versed in sacred texts or in spells, one conversant with sacred knowledge; an epithet of Bṛhas-pati; one of the four principal priests or <i>ṛtvijas</i> (the other three being the Hotṛ, Adhvaryu, and Udgātṛ, q. q. v. v.; he had the supervision of the sacrifice and was required to know the three Vedas; as the most learned of the priests he had to set right any mistake or remedy any defect in the ritual; at a later period functions based especially on the Atharva-veda were assigned to him; his three Puruṣas or assistants were the Brāhmaṇācchaṃsin, Āgnīdhra, and Potṛ); Brahmā or the Supreme Being regarded as a person, (in the later mythology he is held to be the first deity of the Hindū triad and the Creator of the world; he never appears to have become an object of general worship, though a qualified reverence is paid to him in conjunction with other deities; the <i>sapta Brahmāṇaḥ,</i> or seven Brahmās, are the seven Prajā-patis, viz. Marīci, Atri, Aṅgiras, Pulastya, Pulaha, Kratu, and Vasiṣṭha); a lifetime of Brahmā (<i>= Brahmaṇa</i> <i>āyuḥ</i>); the sun; an epithet of Śiva; the Veda (?); intellect (<i>= buddhi</i>); N. of a star, <lang n='greek'>δ</lang> Aurigæ; epithet of a particular astronomical Yoga; N. of the servant of the tenth Arhat of the present Ava-sarpiṇī; N. of a magician; of the ninth Muhūrta; [cf. Zend <nsi>bareśma.</nsi> In giving the meaning of the following words compounded with <i>brahman,</i> the N. Brahman in the crude form will be used in all cases where the distinction between the neut. Brahma and the masc. Brahmā is not clearly determinable.] <i>—Brahma-ṛṣi,</i> see <i>brahmarṣi</i>. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>kanya</i> or <i>brahma-kanyaka,</i> Clerodendrum Siphonanthus; (<i>kā</i>), f. ‘daughter of Brahmā,’ the goddess Sarasvatī. <i>—Brahma-kara, as,</i> m. an impost paid to the priestly class. <i>—Brahma-karman, a,</i> n. the office of Brahman or presiding priest; the work or office of the Brāhmans, the religious duties of the priestly caste. <i>—Brahmakarma-prakāśaka, as,</i> m. an epithet of Go-pāla (i. e. Kṛṣṇa). <i>—Brahma-karma-</i> <i>samādhi, is, is, i,</i> occupied with and meditating upon the Supreme Spirit. <i>—Brahma-kalā,</i> f. an epithet of Dākṣāyaṇī who dwells in the heart of men. <i>—Brahma-kalpa, as, ā, am,</i> like Brahman or the Supreme Being; (<i>as</i>), m. the age of Brahman, epithet of a particular period of time. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>kāṇḍa, am,</i> n. <i>= jñāna-kāṇḍa,</i> that inner portion of the Veda which relates to spiritual knowledge or the knowledge of Brahma, (opposed to <i>karma-</i> <i>kāṇḍa</i> or the knowledge of rites and ceremonies); N. of a work or section of a work by Bhartṛ-hari. <i>—Brahma-kāya, ās,</i> m. pl., N. of a particular class of deities. <i>—Brahmakāyika, as, ī, am,</i> belonging to the class of deities called Brahma-kāyas. <i>—Brahma-kāra, as, ā, am,</i> Ved. making prayers, offering prayers; (Sāy.) <i>= annasya havir-lakṣa-</i> <i>ṇasya kartā,</i> preparing sacrificial food. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>kāṣṭha,</i> the plant Thespesia Populnea; a mulberry tree. <i>—Brahma-kileya (?), as,</i> m., N. of a man. <i>—Brahma-kilbiṣa, am,</i> n., Ved. an offence against Brāhmans. <i>—Brahma-kuṇḍa, am,</i> n., N. of a sacred pool. <i>—Brahma-kuśā,</i> f. a species of plant (<i>= aja-modā;</i> cf. <i>brahma-kośī</i>). <i>—Brahma-kūṭa,</i> <i>as,</i> m., N. of a sacred mountain. <i>—Brahma-kūrca,</i> a particular kind of penance. <i>—Brahma-kṛt, t, t, t,</i> making or offering prayers, singing hymns of praise (Sāy. <i>= stota-kṛt</i>); one who prays, a devout worshipper (Ved.); (<i>t</i>), m. an epithet of Indra (‘making pious or devout ?,’ Ved.); an epithet of Viṣṇu. <i>—Brahma-kṛta, as,</i> m., N. of a man. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>kṛti, is,</i> f., Ved. the making of prayers, praying, devotion (Sāy. <i>= kriyamāṇaṃ stotram</i>). <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-ketu, us,</i> m., N. of a man. <i>—Brahma-kośa,</i> <i>as,</i> m. receptacle or treasury of the Brahman, i. e. of the sacred word or text, &c.; (<i>ī</i>), f. a species of plant (<i>= aja-modā;</i> cf. <i>brahma-kuśā</i>). <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>kṣetra, am,</i> n., N. of a sacred district. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>khaṇḍa, am,</i> n., N. of the first book of the Brahmavaivarta-Purāṇa. <i>—Brahma-gandha, as,</i> m., Ved. the odour or perfume of Brahman. <i>—Brahma-gar-</i> <i>bha, as,</i> m. the embryo of a Brāhman (?); N. of a law-giver; (<i>ā</i>), f. a species of plant, Polanisia Icosandra. <i>—Brahma-gavī,</i> f., Ved. a cow belonging to a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-gāyatrī,</i> f., N. of a particular magical formula. <i>—Brahma-gārgya, as,</i> m., N. of a man. <i>—Brahma-giri, is,</i> m., N. of a mountain. <i>—Brahma-gītā, ās,</i> f. pl., N. of particular verses ascribed to Brahmā (and given in Mahā-bh. Anuśāsana-p. 2146-2152); N. of a work forming chapters 6-9 of the Jñāna-khaṇḍa of the Śiva-Purāṇa and treating of the Vedānta and Yoga systems. <i>—Brahmagītā-vyākhyā,</i> f., N. of a commentary by Mādhava on the Brahma-gītā. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-gītikā,</i> f. ‘the song of Brahmā,’ a N. of certain verses. <i>—Brahma-gupta, as,</i> m., N. of a son of Brahmā by the wife of the Vidyā-dhara Bhīma; of an astronomer born A. D. 598; of a chief of the Bhakta sect; of a Trigarta-ṣaṣṭha, (in this sense also read <i>brāhmagupta</i>); (<i>ās</i>), m. pl., N. of a race. <i>—Brahmaguptīya, as,</i> m. a prince of the Brahma-guptas. <i>—Brahma-gola, as,</i> m. ‘the globe of Brahman,’ the universe. <i>—Brahma-gaurava,</i> <i>am,</i> n. the potency of the weapon given by the god Brahmā (Bhaṭṭi-kāvya IX. 76). <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>granthi, is,</i> m. a term applied to a particular joint of the body. <i>—Brahma-graha, as,</i> m. <i>= brahma-</i> <i>rākṣasa,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-grāhin, ī, iṇī, i,</i> Ved. worthy to receive that which is holy; (also read <i>brahmārgha.</i>) <i>—Brahma-ghātaka, as,</i> m. the slayer or murderer of a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-ghā-</i> <i>tin, ī, inī, i,</i> slaying a Brāhman; (<i>ī</i>), m. (according to a Scholiast) an epithet of Bhṛgu; (<i>inī</i>), f. a woman on the second day of the menses. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>ghoṣa, as,</i> m. ‘prayer-sound,’ the murmur arising from the recital of prayers; the sacred word, the text of the Veda; the reading or repeating of the Veda. <i>—Brahma-ghna, as, ī, am,</i> slaying a Brāhman; (<i>as</i>), m. the slayer or murderer of a Brāhman; (<i>ī</i>), f. the plant Aloe Perfoliata. <i>—Brahma-cakra,</i> <i>am,</i> n. the wheel of Brahman, circle of the universe (Ved.); epithet of a particular magical circle. <i>—Brahma-carya, am,</i> n. sacred study, religious studentship, the condition of a young Brāhman or student in the first period of his life [cf. <i>āśrama,</i> <i>brahma-cārin</i>]; religious self-restraint, pious austerity, the controlling of the senses, abstinence, chastity, sanctity; (<i>as</i>), m. a religious student; (<i>ā</i>), f. chastity. <i>—Brahmacarya-vat, ān, atī, at,</i> leading the life of a religious student, practicing chastity. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>macarya-vrata, am,</i> n. a vow of chastity. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>macarya-skhalana, am,</i> n. falling or deviating from chastity, incontinence. <i>—Brahma-cāraṇī,</i> f. <i>= bhārgī,</i> Clerodendrum Siphonanthus; (a wrong form for <i>brahma-cāriṇī.</i>) <i>—Brahma-cārika, am,</i> n. religious studentship. <i>—Brahma-cārin, ī, iṇī, i,</i> studying sacred learning; practicing continence or chastity; (<i>ī</i>), m. a Brāhman who practices chastity, especially a religious student (or young Brāhman in the first <i>āśrama</i> or period of his life [cf. <i>āśrama</i>] from the time of his investiture with the sacrificial thread till he marries and becomes a householder, or one who remains with his spiritual teacher studying the Veda and observing the duties of a student, cf. Manu II. 219; the title of Brahma-cārin is also given to a particular class of ascetics, and to Pandits learned in the Veda, and by the Tantras to persons whose chief virtue is the observance of continence; in Atharva-veda XI. 5. great powers are ascribed to the Brahma-cārin; he appears in some particulars to be identified with the Supreme Being, and is even said to be the source of the <i>brahma jyeṣṭham</i> or primitive Veda); N. of a Gandharva; an epithet of Skanda; of Śiva; (<i>ī</i>), f. a woman observing a vow of chastity; an epithet of Durgā; N. of various plants, Clerodendrum Siphonanthus; <i>= karuṇī;</i> Thespesia Populnea. <i>—Brahma-codana, as, ī, am,</i> Ved. inciting or encouraging prayer; urging or inciting Brāhmans; (according to Mahī-dhara <i>= brāh-</i> <i>maṇānāṃ yajñam prati prerakaḥ.</i>) <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>ja, as,</i> m. ‘sprung from that which is holy,’ an epithet of Kārttikeya; (<i>ās</i>), m. pl. (with Jainas) N. of a class of divinities enumerated among the Kalpabhavas. <i>—Brahma-ja-jña, as, ā, am,</i> Ved. begotten by and knowing Brahman; knowing what is produced by Brahman, i. e. knowing all things (?). <i>—Brahma-jaṭā</i> or <i>brahma-jaṭī,</i> f. the plant Artemisia Indica. <i>—Brahma-janman, a,</i> n. divine or spiritual birth, the second birth effected by sacred study or knowledge, investiture with the sacred thread; (<i>ā, ā, a</i>), begotten by or sprung from Brahman (said of Prajā-pati). <i>—Brahma-japa, as,</i> m., Ved., N. of a particular form of prayer. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-jāmala = brahma-yāmala,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>jāyā,</i> f., Ved. the wife of a Brāhman; (Juhū Brahma-jāyā is the reputed authoress of the hymn Ṛg-veda X. 109.) <i>—Brahma-jāra, as,</i> m. the paramour of a Brāhman's wife. <i>—Brahma-jīvin, ī,</i> <i>inī, i,</i> living by sacred knowledge, gaining a livelihood by religious learning; (<i>ī</i>), m. a mercenary Brāhman (who converts his religious duties into a trade, performing sacrifice, teaching the Veda &c. for hire). <i>—Brahma-juṣṭa, as, ā, am,</i> Ved. gratified by prayer or devotion. <i>—Brahma-jūta, as, ā,</i> <i>am,</i> Ved. urged on by prayer, incited by devotion; (Sāy.) <i>= stotreṇākṛṣṭaḥ,</i> attracted by a hymn of praise. <i>—Brahma-jña, as, ā, am,</i> knowing sacred things, one who has spiritual wisdom or who knows Brahma as the one all-pervading Spirit, a sage; (<i>as</i>), m. an epithet of Viṣṇu; of Kārttikeya. <i>—Brahma-jñāna, am,</i> n. divine knowledge, true knowledge of the Deity or of the Veda, knowledge of the universal permeation of one Spirit as taught by the Vedānta, spiritual wisdom. <i>—Brahmajñānin,</i> <i>ī, inī, i,</i> possessing true knowledge of the Deity, having true spiritual knowledge; [cf. <i>brahma-</i> <i>jñāna.</i>] <i>—Brahma-jya, as, ā, am,</i> Ved. annoying or using violence against a Brāhman, oppressing a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-jyeya, am,</i> n., Ved. the act of annoying or using violence against a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-jyeṣṭha, as,</i> m. the elder brother of Brahmā; (<i>as, ā, am</i>), Ved. having Brahman for the first or chief. <i>—Brahma-jyotis,</i> n. the splendor of Brahman, brightness of the Deity, (also written <i>brahma jyotis</i>); an epithet of Śiva; (<i>is, is, is</i>), Ved. having the splendor of Brahman, having the splendor of the sacred office; (according to a Scholiast) having the splendor of a presiding priest. — 1. <i>brahmaṇ-vat, ān, atī, at,</i> Ved. accompanied by prayer, devout; having sacred acts; containing the word Brahman; including or representing the priesthood; (<i>ān</i>), m. an epithet of Agni; (<i>atī</i>), f. an epithet of Iṣṭakā. <i>—2. brahmaṇ-vat,</i> ind., Ved. like a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-tattva, am,</i> n. the true knowledge of Brahma or the Supreme Spirit. <i>—Brahma-tarka-stava, as,</i> m., N. of a Vedānta work by Appayya-dīkṣita. <i>—Brahmatarkastava-</i> <i>vivaraṇa, am,</i> n., N. of a commentary on the Brahma-tarka-stava. <i>—Brahma-tas,</i> ind. from the Brāhmanical caste, from the Brāhmans. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>tā,</i> f. the state or condition of a Brāhman, ‘Brāhmanhood;’ the state or nature of Brahma or of the Supreme Spirit, divine nature. <i>—Brahma-tāla, as,</i> m. Ligusticum Ajowan. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-dātṛ, tā, trī, tṛ, = brahma-da</i>. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>dāna, am,</i> n. the gift of sacred knowledge. <i>—1. brah-</i> <i>ma-dāya, as,</i> m. [cf. 1. <i>dāya</i>], the gift of sacred knowledge, instruction in the Vedas; (<i>as, ā, am</i>), imparting or teaching sacred knowledge. <i>—2. brah-</i> <i>ma-dāya, as,</i> m. of a king who reigned in the beginning of the fifteenth century. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>dina, am,</i> n. a day of Brahmā. <i>—Brahma-deya,</i> <i>as, ā, am,</i> given (in marriage) after the manner of Brāhmans, married according to the Brāhmo vivāha (see Manu III. 27). <i>—Brahma-daitya, am,</i> n. a Brāhman changed into a Daitya. <i>—Brahma-dvāra,</i> <i>am,</i> n. ingress into Brahma or the Supreme Spirit. <i>—Brahma-dviṣ, ṭ, ṭ, ṭ,</i> or <i>brahma-dveṣin, ī,</i> <i>iṇī, i,</i> ‘prayer-hating,’ hostile to devotion and holy acts, hating religion, godless, impious (said of men and demons; (<i>as</i>), m. the mulberry tree. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-nīḍa, am,</i> n. the resting-place of Brahman or of ‘the holy.’ <i>—Brahma-nutta, as, ā, am,</i> Ved. cast out through the efficacy of a sacred text. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>pati, is,</i> m., Ved. <i>= brahmaṇas-pati,</i> q. v. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-pattra, am,</i> n. ‘Brahman's leaf,’ i. e. the leaf of Butea Frondosa; [cf. <i>brahma-pādapa.</i>] <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-patha, as,</i> m. the way to Brahman or the Supreme Spirit; the way to Brahmā. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>pada, am,</i> n. the place of Brahman or the Supreme Spirit, the place or nature of spiritual being; the station or rank of Brahmā; the station or rank of a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-pannaga, as,</i> m., N. of a Marut; (also read <i>bahu-pannaga.</i>) <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>pariṣadya = brahma-pārṣadya,</i> q. v. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-parṇī,</i> f. a species of plant, Hemionitis Cordifolia <i>(= pṛśni-parṇī)</i>. <i>—Brahma-parvata, am,</i> n. ‘mountain of Brahmā,’ N. of a place. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>palāśa, ās,</i> m. pl., N. of a school of the Atharvaveda; (also written <i>brāhmapalāśa.</i>) <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>pavitra, as,</i> m. Kuśa grass, Poa Cynosuroides. <i>—Brahma-pādapa, as,</i> m. ‘tree of Brahman,’ the tree Butea Frondosa. <i>—Brahma-pārṣadya, ās,</i> m. pl. (with Buddhists) ‘retinue of Brahmā,’ N. of a class of divinities. <i>—Brahma-pāśa, as,</i> m. ‘noose of Brahmā,’ N. of a mythical weapon, a weapon given by Brahmā (Bhaṭṭi-kāvya IX. 75). <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>pitṛ, tā,</i> m. ‘father of Brahmā,’ Viṣṇu; [cf. <i>brahma-nābha.</i>] <i>—Brahma-piśāca, as,</i> m. <i>=</i> <i>brahma-rākṣasa,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-putra, as,</i> m. the son of a priest or Brāhman (Ved.); (Sāy.) <i>=</i> <i>brāhmaṇācchaṃsin,</i> q. v.; a son of Brahmā (as Sanat-kumāra, Manu, &c.); N. of a river (rising at the eastern extremity of the Himālaya in Thibet, flowing through Assam, where it is joined by the Sanpoo, and falling with the Ganges into the Bay of Bengal); of a place of pilgrimage (probably the source of the Brahma-putra river); of a lake; N. of a sacred district; a kind of vegetable poison; (<i>ī</i>), f. ‘daughter of Brahmā,’ an epithet of the river Sarasvatī [cf. <i>brahma-nadī</i>]; a kind of esculent root <i>(=</i> <i>vārāhī)</i>. <i>—Brahmaputra-tā,</i> f. the being a son of Brahman, divine sonship. <i>—Brahma-pura, am,</i> n. ‘city of Brahmā,’ N. of a city in heaven; of a city on earth; of a kingdom; a term applied to the heart (Ved.); a term applied to the body (Ved.); (<i>ī</i>), f. the city of Brahmā (in heaven), the capital of Brahmā on the mountain Kailāsa; N. of any city the inhabitants of which are mostly Brāhmans; an epithet of Benares; N. of a peak in the Himālaya range. <i>—Brahma-puraka, ās,</i> m. pl., N. of a people. <i>—Brahma-purāṇa, am,</i> n., N. of one of the eighteen Purāṇas so called as revealed by Brahmā to Dakṣa, (this Purāṇa is sometimes placed first and therefore called Ādi-Purāṇa; its main object appears to be the promotion of the worship of Kṛṣṇa.) <i>—Brahma-puruṣa, as,</i> m., Ved. an assistant of the Brahman or chief priest, see <i>brahman;</i> a minister of Brahman (said of the five vital airs); <i>= brahma-</i> <i>rākṣasa,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-purogava, as, ī, am,</i> Ved. preceded by Brahman or ‘the holy.’ <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>purohita, as,</i> m., Ved. having the sacerdotal class for a Puro-hita; (<i>ās</i>), m. pl. ‘the high priests of Brahman,’ (with Buddhists) epithet of a class of divinities. <i>—Brahma-puṣpi, is,</i> m., N. of a man; (probably wrongly for <i>brāhmapuṣpa,</i> a patronymic fr. <i>brahma-puṣpa.</i>) <i>—Brahma-pūta, as, ā, am,</i> Ved. purified by devotion; purified by Brahman (Brahma or Brahmā). <i>—Brahma-pralaya, as,</i> m. the universal destruction that takes place at the end of every hundred years of Brahmā, in which even Brahmā himself is swallowed up. <i>—Brahma-prasūta,</i> <i>as, ā, am,</i> Ved. urged or requested by a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-prāpti, is,</i> f. obtainment of Brahma, absorption of the soul into the divine essence. <i>—Brahma-priya, as, ā, am,</i> loving or delighting in devotion. <i>—Brahma-prī, īs, īs, i,</i> Ved. loving or delighting in devotion; (Sāy.) <i>= somalakṣaṇenān-</i> <i>nena prītaḥ</i>. <i>—Brahma-badha,</i> see <i>brahma-va-</i> <i>dha</i>. <i>—Brahma-bandhava, am,</i> n., Ved. (probably) the office or occupation of a priest's assistant; (perhaps a wrong form for <i>brāhmabandhava.</i>) <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-bandhu, us,</i> m. ‘the kinsman of a Brāhman,’ an unworthy member of the Brāhmanical class, a contemptuous term for a Brāhman; a Brāhman only in name; (according to Sāy.) a Brāhman who does not perform his Sandhyā or devotions at sunrise and sunset. <i>—Brahmabandhu-tā,</i> f. the being a Brāhman only in name. <i>—Brahma-bala, as,</i> m., N. of a man. <i>—Brahma-bali, is,</i> m., N. of a teacher of the Atharva-veda. <i>—Brahma-bileya (?), as,</i> m., N. of a man; (also written <i>brahma-vileya.</i>) <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-bīja, am,</i> n. ‘germ of religious knowledge,’ an epithet of the mystical syllable <i>Om;</i> a mulberry tree. <i>—Brahma-bodhyā,</i> f., N. of a river; (also read <i>brahma-vedhyā.</i>) <i>—Brahma-bruvāṇa, as, ā, am,</i> calling one's self a Brāhman, professing or pretending to be a Brāhman; [cf. <i>bruva.</i>] <i>—Brahma-bhadrā,</i> f. a species of plant <i>(= trāyamāṇā)</i>. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>bhavana, am,</i> n. the abode of Brahman. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>bhāga, as,</i> m., Ved. the share of a priest, the portion of a Brahman or chief priest; a mulberry tree. <i>—Brahma-bhāva, as,</i> m. the becoming Brahma, entrance or re-absorption into the Supreme Spirit. <i>—Brahma-bhāvana, as, ā, am,</i> revealing or imparting religious knowledge. <i>—Brahma-bhid, t, t,</i> <i>t,</i> ‘dividing Brahma,’ making many Brahmas out of the one Brahma. <i>—Brahma-bhuvana, am,</i> n. the world of Brahmā. <i>—Brahma-bhūta, as, ā, am,</i> become (one with) Brahma or the universal spirit, entered into Brahma; (<i>am</i>), n. that which is identified with the universal spirit, condition of Brahma (?) . <i>—Brahma-bhūti, is,</i> f. twilight. <i>—Brahma-bhū-</i> <i>mi-jā,</i> f. ‘growing in the land of Brahmā,’ N. of a species of plant. <i>—Brahma-bhūya, am,</i> n. the becoming (one with) Brahma, identification or identity with Brahma, absorption into Brahma; final felicity, ultimate happiness; the state or rank of a Brāhman, ‘Brāhmanhood.’ <i>—Brahmabhūya-tva, am,</i> n. the becoming one with Brahma; the condition of a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-bhūyas, ān, asī, as,</i> becoming one with Brahma, being absorbed into Brahma; (<i>as</i>), n. absorption into Brahma. <i>—Brahma-maṅ-</i> <i>gala-devatā,</i> f. an epithet of Lakṣmī. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>maṭha, as,</i> m. ‘the college of Brahman,’ N. of a college of theology in Kaśmīra. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>maṇḍūkī,</i> f. Clerodendrum Siphonanthus; (also written <i>brahma-māṇḍūkī;</i> cf. <i>brāhmī.</i>) <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-mati, is,</i> m. (with Buddhists) N. of a demon. <i>—Brahma-maya, as, ī, am,</i> consisting or made of Brahma, identified with Brahma, belonging or relating to the Veda, (according to Malli-nātha on Kumāra-s. V. 30 <i>= vaidika</i>); belonging to or fit for a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-maha, as,</i> m. a feast in honour of the Brāhmans. <i>—Brahma-māṇḍūkī</i> <i>= brahma-maṇḍūkī,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-mitra, as, </i> <i>ā, am,</i> having Brahman for a friend, befriended by Brahman; having the Brāhmans for friends; (<i>as</i>), m., N. of a Muni. <i>—Brahma-mīmāṃsā,</i> f. ‘investigation into Brahma or the spiritual doctrine of the Veda,’ N. of the Vedānta philosophy treating of the Supreme Spirit (<i>= uttara-mīmāṃsā, śārīraka-</i> <i>mīmāṃsā, vedānta,</i> q. q. v. v.). <i>—Brahmamīmāṃ-</i> <i>sā-bhāṣya, am,</i> n., N. of a commentary by Śaṅkarācārya. <i>—Brahmamīmāṃsā-bhāṣyakāra, as,</i> m. ‘commentator on the Brahma-mīmāṃsā,’ an epithet of Śaṅkarācārya. <i>—Brahmamīmāṃsābhā-</i> <i>ṣya-vivaraṇa, am,</i> n., N. of a commentary by Ānanda-tīrtha on Śaṅkarācārya's Brahmamīmāṃsābhāṣya. <i>—Brahma-mūrti, is, is, i,</i> having the figure of Brahmā, in the form of Brahmā. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-mūrdha-bhṛt, t,</i> m. ‘carrying the head of Brahmā,’ an epithet of Śiva (as having in a dispute cut off one of Brahmā's heads). <i>—Brahma-mekhala,</i> <i>as,</i> m. the plant Saccharum Munjia (<i>muñja</i>), of which the sacred thread of a Brāhman is made. <i>—Brahma-medhyā,</i> f., N. of a river. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>yajña, as,</i> m. ‘the offering of prayer or of repeating the Veda,’ repeating by heart or recitation of a sacred text, teaching and repeating the Vedas (regarded as one of the five Mahā-yajñas or great sacrifices, see Manu III. 70, where Kullūka explains <i>brahma-</i> <i>yajña</i> by <i>adhyāpana</i> and <i>adhyayana</i>); N. of the thirty-first chapter of the Sṛṣṭi-khaṇḍa of the Padma-Purāṇa; [cf. <i>brahma-sattra.</i>] <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>yajña-māhātmya, am,</i> n., N. of a chapter of the Purāṇa-sarvasva. <i>—Brahmayajña-vidhi, is,</i> m., N. of a chapter of Mādhava's Parāśara-smṛti. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>mayajñādi-vidhi (°ña-ād°), is,</i> m., N. of a work. <i>—Brahma-yaśas, as,</i> or <i>brahma-yaśasa, am,</i> n., Ved. the glory or majesty of Brahman. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>yaśasin, ī, inī, i,</i> Ved. renowned for sanctity. <i>—Brahma-yaṣṭi, is,</i> or <i>brahma-yaṣṭikā,</i> or <i>brahma-yaṣṭī,</i> f. the plant Clerodendrum Siphonanthus; (probably) <i>= brahma-yajña,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>yātu, us,</i> m. epithet of a particular Yātu; [cf. <i>deva-yātu.</i>] <i>—Brahma-yāmala,</i> N. of a Tantra; (also written <i>brahma-jāmala.</i>) <i>—Brahma-yuga,</i> <i>am,</i> n. the age of the Brāhmans, (opposed to <i>kṣa-</i> <i>trasya yugam,</i> the age of the Kṣatriyas, Hari-vaṃśa 11808.) <i>—Brahma-yuj, k, k, k,</i> Ved. harnessed by prayer or devotion (i. e. bringing Indra in answer to the prayers of men, said of the horses of that deity; (<i>is, is, i</i>), having the original source or home in Brahma; descended or sprung from Brahmā; (<i>is, ī</i>), f., N. of a place of pilgrimage; (<i>is</i>), m., N. of a mountain <i>(= brahma-giri)</i>. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>yoni-stha, as, ā, am,</i> intent on the means of attaining sacred knowledge or the supreme godhead, (according to Kullūka on Manu X. 74 <i>= brahma-</i> <i>prāpti-kāraṇa-brahma-dhyāna-niṣṭha.</i>) <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-rakṣas, as,</i> n., N. of a kind of evil demon (<i>=</i> <i>brahma-rākṣasa,</i> q. v.). <i>—Brahma-ratna, am,</i> n. a valuable present made to Brāhmans. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>ratha, as,</i> m. the chariot or carriage of a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-randhra, am,</i> n. a suture or aperture in the crown of the head and through which the soul is said to escape on death. <i>—Brahma-rasa, as,</i> m., Ved. the savour of Brahman, the savour of divine knowledge. <i>—Brahma-rākṣasa, as,</i> m. a kind of evil demon, a fiend of the Brāhmanical class, the ghost of a Brāhman who in his lifetime indulged a haughty and disdainful spirit; a species of plant commonly called Thorarohiḍā; (<i>ī</i>), f. epithet of one of the nine Samidhs. <i>—Brahma-rāja, as,</i> m., N. of a king; of a man. <i>—Brahma-rāta, as,</i> m. ‘given by Brahmā,’ an epithet of Śuka; N. of the father of Yājñavalkya. <i>—Brahma-rātra, as,</i> m. ‘the night of Brahmā,’ epithet of a particular hour of night. <i>—Brahma-rātri, is,</i> m. an epithet of Yājñavalkya; (an incorrect form for <i>brāhmarāti.</i>) <i>—Brahma- </i> <i>rāśi, is,</i> m. the whole circle of sacred knowledge, whole mass of the sacred text; ‘a mass of holiness,’ an epithet of Paraśu-rāma; a particular constellation, (according to a Scholiast <i>= śravaṇa,</i> q. v.) <i>—Brahma-rīti, is,</i> f. a kind of brass. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-rūpiṇī,</i> f. a species of plant (commonly called Bādāṅgula). <i>—Brahma-rekhā,</i> f. ‘line of Brahmā,’ the lines or destiny written by Brahmā on the forehead of every creature, the predestined lot of a man. <i>—Brahmarṣi (°ma-ṛ°), is,</i> m. ‘Brāhmanical sage,’ epithet of a particular class of sages [cf. <i>ṛṣi</i>] supposed to belong to the Brāhmanical caste (as Vasiṣṭha, &c.; higher than Maharṣi, q. v.; also written <i>brahma-ṛṣi,</i> see Grammar 38. <i>h</i>). <i>—Brahmarṣi-tā,</i> f. or <i>brahmarṣi-</i> <i>tva, am,</i> n. the being a Brahmarṣi, the rank of a sage of the Brāhmanical class. <i>—Brahmarṣi-deśa,</i> <i>as,</i> m. ‘the country of the Brahmarṣis,’ including Kuru-kṣetra and the country of the Matsyas, Pañcālas, and Śūrasenakas (see Manu II. 19). <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-lakṣaṇa-vākyārtha (°ya-ar°),</i> N. of an abridgement of the Vedānta-sudhā-rahasya. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-likhita, am,</i> n. or <i>brahma-lekha, as,</i> m. ‘Brahmā's writing,’ a man's destiny written on his forehead <i>(= brahma-rekhā)</i>. <i>—Brahma-loka, as,</i> m. the world of Brahmā, i. e. the heaven or place of residence of Brahmā, (a division of the universe and one of the supposed residences of pious spirits.) <i>—Brahma-vaktṛ, tā,</i> m. a proclaimer of religious truths, a teacher of the Veda. <i>—1. brahma-vat, ān,</i> <i>atī, at,</i> possessed of Brahma; possessing religious learning. <i>—2. brahma-vat,</i> ind. according to the sacred text, according to the Veda. <i>—Brahma-vada</i> or <i>brahma-vala, ās,</i> m. pl., N. of a school; (probably an incorrect form.) <i>—Brahma-vadya, am,</i> n. knowledge or declaration of Brahma, <i>= brahmodya,</i> q. v.; (<i>as, ā, am</i>), in <i>brahma-vadyā kathā,</i> see Vopa-deva XXVI. 21. <i>—Brahma-vadha, as,</i> m. or <i>brahma-vadhyā,</i> f. the murder of a Brāhman. <i>—Brahmavadhyā-kṛta, am,</i> n. an act of Brāhmanicide, the crime of killing a Brāhman. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-vani, is, is, i,</i> Ved. (according to Mahī-dhara) devoted to the Brāhmans. <i>—Brahma-varcas,</i> see <i>brahma-varcasa</i>. <i>—Brahma-varcasa, am,</i> n. divine glory or splendor; eminence in holiness or in sacred knowledge, spiritual pre-eminence, holiness resulting from the study and observance of the Vedas; the sanctity or superhuman power of a Brāhman. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-varcasin</i> or <i>brahma-varcasvin, ī, inī, i,</i> eminent in religious learning, holy; illumined by the Vedas; (<i>ī</i>), m. an illustrious priest, holy Brāhman, (Mahī-dhara <i>= yajñādhyayana-śīlo brāhmaṇaḥ.</i>) <i>—Brahma-varcasya, as, ā, am,</i> see Vārttika to Pāṇ. V. 1, 39. <i>—Brahma-varta, as,</i> m. <i>= brahmā-</i> <i>varta,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-vardhana, am,</i> n. copper (which is considered peculiarly suitable for sacrificial utensils). <i>—Brahma-vala = brahma-vada,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-vallī,</i> f. Brahmā's tendril or creeper. <i>—Brahmavallī-lipi,</i> N. of a work. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>vāṭīya, as, ā, am,</i> epithet of a kind of Muni. <i>—Brahma-vāda, as,</i> m., Ved. speaking of sacred matters, declaring or teaching spiritual knowledge, citing the Vedas; <i>(as, ā, am), = brahma-vādin.</i> <i>—Brahmavādi-tva, am,</i> n. the being an expounder of the Veda. <i>—Brahma-vādin, ī, inī, i,</i> one who recites the Veda, a defender or expounder of the Veda, a theologian, speaking of or discussing sacred matters; one who asserts that all things are Brahma, a follower of the Vedānta system of philosophy. <i>—Brahma-vādya, am,</i> n., Ved. rivalry in sacred knowledge or in magical power, (according to the commentator, also <i>as, ā, am;</i> cf. <i>brahma-</i> <i>vadya, brahmodya.</i>) <i>—Brahma-vāluka, am,</i> n., N. of a Tīrtha. <i>—Brahma-vāsa, as,</i> m. the abode of Brahmā, the heaven of Brahmā. <i>—Brahma-vā-</i> <i>has, ās, ās, as,</i> Ved. one to whom prayers are offered (said of Indra); (Sāy.) <i>= stotreṇa prāpya-</i> <i>māṇaḥ,</i> obtained by prayer; <i>= stotrasya vāhakaḥ,</i> the accepter of prayer. <i>—Brahmavit-tva, am,</i> n. (fr. <i>brahma-vid</i>), knowledge of Brahma or the Supreme Spirit. <i>—Brahma-vid, t, t, t,</i> or <i>brahma- </i> <i>vida, as, ā, am,</i> knowing Brahma or the Supreme Spirit, a theologian, philosopher, sage; skilled in sacred spells or magical charms. <i>—Brahma-vidyā,</i> f. knowledge of ‘the holy’ or of Brahma; knowledge of the Supreme Spirit or Soul of the Universe; N. of an Upaniṣad. <i>—Brahmavidyā-tīrtha, as,</i> m., N. of an author. <i>—Brahmavidyābharaṇa (°yā-</i> <i>ābh°), am,</i> n., N. of a commentary by Advaitānanda on the Śārīraka-mīmāṃsā-bhāṣya. <i>—Brahma-vid-</i> <i>vas, vān, uṣī, vas,</i> Ved. one who knows Brahma, knowing the Supreme Spirit. <i>—Brahma-vidviṣ, ṭ,</i> <i>ṭ, ṭ, = brahma-dviṣ,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-vindu, us,</i> m. a drop of saliva sputtered while reciting the Veda; N. of an Upaniṣad connected with the Atharvaveda. <i>—Brahma-vivardhana, as,</i> m. ‘increasing religious knowledge,’ an epithet of Viṣṇu. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-viśeṣa-citta-paripṛcchā,</i> f., N. of a Buddhist Sūtra work. <i>—Brahma-vṛkṣa, as,</i> m. ‘the divine tree’ or ‘Brahma regarded as a tree;’ the Palāśa tree, Butea Frondosa; the glomerous fig-tree, Ficus Glomerata. <i>—Brahma-vṛtti, is,</i> f. the livelihood or means of subsistence of a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>vṛddha, as, ā, am,</i> Ved. become great by devotion, increased by prayer. <i>—Brahma-vṛddhi, is,</i> m., N. of a man. <i>—Brahma-vṛnda, am,</i> n. a company or assemblage of Brāhmans; (<i>ā</i>), f., N. of the city of Brahmā. <i>—Brahma-veda, as,</i> m. ‘the Veda of sacred spells or charms,’ a N. of the Atharva-veda; the Veda of the Brāhmans, (opposed to <i>kṣatra-</i> <i>veda,</i> q. v.); knowledge of Brahma, monotheism; knowledge of the Vedas. <i>—Brahmaveda-maya, as,</i> <i>ī, am,</i> consisting of the Brahma-veda. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>vedi, is,</i> f. ‘the altar of Brahmā,’ N. of the country between the five lakes of Rāma in Kuru-kṣetra. <i>—Brahma-vedin, ī, inī, i, = brahma-vid,</i> knowing or acquainted with the Vedas or spiritual knowledge. <i>—Brahma-vedhyā,</i> another form for <i>brah-</i> <i>ma-bodhyā,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-vaivarta</i> or <i>brahma-</i> <i>vaivartaka, am,</i> n. ‘changes of Brahman’ (who is identified with Kṛṣṇa), N. of a Purāṇa, (this Purāṇa, which is one of the most modern of the eighteen, contains prayers and invocations addressed to Kṛṣṇa, descriptions of Vṛndāvana and Go-loka, with tedious narratives about Kṛṣṇa and his love for the Gopīs and Rādhā.) <i>—Brahma-vrata, am,</i> n., N. of a religious observance; a vow of chastity. <i>—Brahma-śalya, as,</i> m. a species of plant (<i>=</i> <i>soma-valka</i>); the tree Mimosa Arabica. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>śāyin, ī, inī, i,</i> resting or reposing in Brahma. <i>—Brahma-śālā,</i> f. the hall of Brahmā; N. of a sacred place. <i>—Brahma-śāsana, am,</i> n. an edict addressed to the Brāhmans; a command of Brahmā; the command of a Brāhman, <i>= dharma-kīlaka;</i> <i>(as),</i> m., N. of a Grāma. <i>—Brahma-śiras, as,</i> or <i>brahma-śīrṣan, a,</i> n. ‘the head of Brahmā,’ N. of a mythical weapon. <i>—Brahma-śumbhita, as, ā,</i> <i>am,</i> Ved. cleansed by prayer, adorned by devotion. <i>—Brahma-śrī, īs,</i> f., N. of a Sāman. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>śrī-mantra, as,</i> m., N. of a chapter of Kṛṣṇānanda's Tantra-sāra. <i>—Brahma-saṃśita, as, ā, am,</i> Ved. sharpened by prayer or by a sacred text (Sāy. <i>= mantreṇa tīkṣṇī-kṛtaḥ</i>). <i>—Brahma-saṃsad,</i> <i>t,</i> f. Brahman's hall of assembly or court. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-saṃstha, as, ā, am,</i> Ved. wholly devoted to Brahma or to religious knowledge, attaining to union with Brahma. <i>—Brahma-saṃhitā,</i> f. a collection of prayers; N. of a short treatise on the Vedānta system. <i>—Brahmasaṃhitā-vyākhyā,</i> f., N. of a commentary on the Brahma-saṃhitā. <i>—Brahma-satī,</i> f. a N. of the river Sarasvatī. <i>—Brahma-sattra, am,</i> n. the sacrifice or offering of devotion or abstract meditation, absorption in the holy one; study and teaching of the Vedas, the constant repetition of the Vedas or a particular portion of the Vedas which is constantly studied and repeated (Manu II. 106; cf. <i>brahma-</i> <i>yajña</i>) . <i>—Brahma-sattrin, ī, iṇī, i,</i> offering the sacrifice of prayer, absorbed in the holy one. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-sadana, am,</i> n. the seat of the Brahman or chief priest (Ved.); the abode or heaven of Brahmā; N. of a Tīrtha, (in this sense a various reading for <i>veda-vadana.</i>) <i>—Brahma-sadas, as,</i> n. the residence or court of Brahmā. <i>—Brahma-sabhā,</i> f. the hall or court of Brahmā. <i>—Brahma-sambandha,</i> <i>as,</i> m. <i>= brahma-rākṣasa,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahma-sam-</i> <i>bhava, as, ā, am,</i> sprung from Brahman; coming from Brahmā; sprung or descended from Brāhmans; (<i>as</i>), m. (with Jainas) N. of the second black Vāsudeva; of the author of a law-book. <i>—Brahma-saras,</i> <i>as,</i> n. ‘the lake of Brahmā,’ N. of a very sacred bathing-place. <i>—Brahma-sarpa, as,</i> m. ‘the serpent of Brahmā,’ a kind of snake. <i>—Brahma-sava, as,</i> m. ‘divine clarifying process,’ distillation of Soma, (Sāy. <i>brahma = Soma,</i>) or the (Soma) distillation (performed) by Brāhmans; N. of a particular libation. <i>—Brahma-sāgara, as,</i> m., N. of a place. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-sāt,</i> ind. into the state of Brahma, with reference to Brahma. <i>—Brahmasāt-kṛta, as, ā, am,</i> absorbed into the state of Brahma, performed with reference to Brahma. <i>—Brahma-sāma, am,</i> or <i>brahma-sāman, a,</i> n., Ved., N. of a Sāman (sung to a text recited by the Brahman or chief priest or by the Brāhmaṇācchaṃsin). <i>—Brahma-sāyujya,</i> <i>am,</i> n. intimate union or identification with Brahma, entrance into Brahma. <i>—Brahma-sārṣṭitā,</i> f. equality or identification with Brahma, union with the Supreme Spirit, (according to Kullūka <i>= brah-</i> <i>maṇaḥ samāna-gati-tā.</i>) <i>—Brahma-sāvarṇa, as,</i> m., N. of a particular Manu; (<i>am</i>), n., N. of his Manv-antara. <i>—Brahma-sāvarṇi, is,</i> m., N. of the tenth Manu; (also written <i>brahmā-sāvarṇi.</i>) <i>—Brahma-siddhānta, as,</i> m., N. of various astronomical works. <i>—Brahma-siddhi, is,</i> m., N. of a Muni; (<i>is</i>), f., N. of a work by Maṇḍana-miśra. <i>—Brahma-suta, as,</i> m. ‘the son of Brahmā,’ i. e. the Ketu Brahma-daṇḍa. <i>—Brahma-suvarcalā,</i> f. a species of plant (an infusion of which is drunk as a penance for eating anything left by a cat, crow, rat, &c., Manu XI. 159); Helianthus; Clerodendrum Siphonanthus <i>(= brāhmī)</i>. <i>—Brahma-sū, ūs,</i> m. ‘the son of Brahmā,’ an epithet of A-niruddha, son of the god of love; N. of Kāma-deva, the god of love. <i>—Brahma-sūtra, am,</i> n. the sacrificial or Brāhmanical thread worn over the shoulder; a Sūtra work treating of true divine knowledge or of the Vedānta philosophy; N. of a work containing the aphorisms of the Vedānta philosophy ascribed to Bādārāyaṇa or Vyāsa, also denominated Vedāntasūtra and Śārīraka-sūtra, q. q. v. v. <i>—Brahmasūtra-</i> <i>ṛju-vyākhyā,</i> f., N. of a commentary on the Brahma-sūtras by Vijñāna-bhikṣu or Vijñāna-yati. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>masūtra-bhāṣya, am,</i> n., N. of a commentary by Śaṅkarācārya; of a commentary by Ānanda-tīrtha. <i>—Brahmasūtra-vṛtti, is,</i> f., N. of a commentary by Bodhāyana; of a commentary by Bhairavadīkṣita-tilaka. <i>—Brahmasūtrānubhāṣya (°ra-</i> <i>an°), am,</i> n., N. of a commentary by Vallabhācārya. <i>—Brahma-sūtrin, ī, iṇī, i,</i> invested with the Brāhmanical cord. <i>—Brahma-sūnu, us,</i> m. (with Jainas) a sovereign of the race of Ikṣvāku; N. of the twelfth king of Bhārata. <i>—Brahma-sṛj, ṭ,</i> m. ‘the creator of Brahmā,’ an epithet of Śiva. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-soma, as,</i> m., N. of a sage. <i>—Brahma-stamba,</i> <i>as,</i> m. ‘Brahman's post or prop,’ the world. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>ma-stambi, is,</i> m., N. of a man; (probably a wrong form for <i>brāhmastambi,</i> a patronymic fr. <i>brahma-</i> <i>stamba.</i>) <i>—Brahma-steya, am,</i> n. stealing that which is holy, stealing the Veda, obtaining a knowledge of the Veda by illicit means. <i>—Brahma-</i> <i>sthala, am,</i> n., N. of a city, (also read <i>brahma-</i> <i>pura</i>); N. of a village. <i>—Brahma-sthāna, am,</i> n. ‘place or abode of Brahmā,’ N. of a Tīrtha; (probably <i>as,</i> m.), a mulberry tree. <i>—Brahma-sphuṭa-</i> <i>siddhānta, as,</i> m., N. of an astronomical work by Brahma-gupta (whose name is frequently written Brāhma-gupta). <i>—Brahma-sva, am,</i> n. Brāhmanical property, money or lands belonging to Brāhmans. <i>—Brahma-svarūpa, as, ā, am,</i> of the nature of spirit, of the same essence as the godhead. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>masva-hārin, ī, iṇī, i,</i> carrying off or stealing the property of Brāhmans. <i>—Brahma-svāmin, ī,</i> m., N. of a man. <i>—Brahma-hatyā,</i> f. killing a Brāhman, Brāhmanicide, or any crime equally heinous. <i>—Brahma-han, ā, ghnī, a,</i> ‘Brāhmanslaying,’ murdering a Brāhman, the murderer or slayer of a Brāhman. <i>—Brahma-huta, am,</i> n. the oblation or offering to Brāhmans, performance of the rites of hospitality (especially to twice-born guests, <i>= nṛ-yajña, atithi-pūjana,</i> one of the Mahā-yajñas, see Manu III. 74, and cf. <i>brāhmya-</i> <i>huta</i>). <i>—Brahma-hṛdaya, as, am,</i> m. n. the star Capella. <i>—Brahma-hrada, as,</i> m., N. of a lake. <i>—Brahmākṣara (°ma-ak°), am,</i> n. the sacred and mysterious syllable, the syllable <i>Om</i> (regarded as a mystical name of the Deity). <i>—Brahmākṣara-</i> <i>maya, as, ī, am,</i> consisting of sacred syllables. <i>—Brahmāgra-bhū (°ma-ag°), ūs,</i> m. a horse; [cf. <i>brahmātma-bhū.</i>] <i>—Brahmāñjali (°ma-añ°),</i> <i>is,</i> m. ‘homage to the divine,’ joining the hollowed hands together while repeating the Veda (either as an act of homage or to mark by the motion of the hands so placed the accentuation of the Sāma-veda; cf. Manu II. 71); obeisance to a spiritual preceptor at the beginning or end of a repetition of the Veda; [cf. <i>añjali.</i>] <i>—Brahmāñjali-kṛta, as, ā, am,</i> one who has joined the hollowed hands in token of homage to the Veda. <i>—Brahmāṇḍa (°ma-aṇ°),</i> <i>am,</i> n. ‘the egg of Brahmā,’ the mundane egg, the universe, globe, world; N. of a Purāṇa and of an Upa-Purāṇa. <i>—Brahmāṇḍa-purāṇa, am,</i> n., N. of one of the eighteen Purāṇas so called as revealed by Brahmā, and containing an account of the egg of Brahmā and the future Kalpas, (this Purāṇa is supposed to be only extant in a number of unauthentic fragments or Khaṇḍas.) <i>—Brahmāṇḍa-bhāṇḍodara</i> <i>(°ḍa-ud°), am,</i> n. the interior of the vessel-like egg of Brahmā. <i>—Brahmātithi (°ma-at°), is,</i> m., N. of a Kāṇva (author of the hymn Ṛg-veda VIII. 5). <i>—Brahmātma-bhū (°ma-āt°), ūs,</i> m. a horse; [cf. <i>brahmāgra-bhū.</i>] <i>—Brahmādanī (°ma-ad°),</i> f. a species of plant <i>(= haṃsa-padī)</i>. <i>—Brahmā-</i> <i>darśa (°ma-ād°), as,</i> m., N. of a work by Vijñānācārya. <i>—Brahmādi-jātā (°ma-ad°),</i> f. the river Godāvarī; (probably an incorrect form for <i>brahmā-</i> <i>dri-jātā;</i> also written <i>brāhmādri-jātā.</i>) <i>—Brah-</i> <i>mādi-śīrṣa (°ma-ād°),</i> N. of a place; (probably for <i>brahmādri-śīrṣa.</i>) — 1. <i>brahmādya (°ma-</i> <i>ād°), as, ā, am</i> (fr. <i>brahma</i> + 1. <i>ādya,</i> q. v.), beginning with Brahmā (Manu I. 50). <i>—2. brahmādya</i> <i>(°ma-ād°), as, ā, am</i> (fr. <i>brahma</i> + 2. <i>ādya,</i> q. v.), Ved. to be eaten by priests or Brāhmans. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>mādri-jātā,</i> see <i>brahmādi-jātā</i>. <i>—Brahmādhi-</i> <i>gama (°ma-adh°), as,</i> m. or <i>brahmādhigamana,</i> <i>am,</i> n. application or devotion to sacred study, repetition of the Veda. <i>—Brahmādhigamika, as, ā,</i> <i>am,</i> proceeding or derived from the study or repetition of the Veda. <i>—Brahmānanda (°ma-ān°),</i> <i>as,</i> m. ‘joy in Brahma,’ the rapture of absorption into the Supreme Spirit, beatitude, bliss; N. of a man. <i>—Brahmānanda-pañcaka, am,</i> n., N. of the third part of Bhāratī-tīrtha's Pañca-daśī. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>mānanda-bhāratī</i> or <i>brahmānanda-sarasvatī,</i> <i>īs,</i> m., N. of the author of several commentaries. <i>—Brahmānanda-vallī,</i> f., N. of the second Vallī of the Taittirīya Upaniṣad. <i>—Brahmāpeta (°ma-</i> <i>ap°), as,</i> m., N. of one of the seven Rākṣasas said to dwell in the sun during the month Māgha. <i>—Brahmābhyāsa (°ma-abh°), as,</i> m. the study of the Veda. <i>—Brahmāmṛta-varṣiṇī (°ma-am°),</i> f., N. of a commentary by Śrī-rāmānanda on the Brahma-sūtras. <i>—Brahmāmbhas (°ma-am°), as,</i> n. ‘holy water,’ the urine of a cow. <i>—Brahmāyaṇa</i> or <i>brahmāyana (°ma-ay°), as,</i> m. ‘refuge of Brahmā,’ resorted to by Brahmā, epithet of Nārāyaṇa; [cf. <i>tridaśāyana.</i>] <i>—Brahmāyatana (°ma-āy°), am,</i> n., Ved. a temple of Brahmā. <i>—Brahmāyus (°ma-</i> <i>āy°), us,</i> m., N. of a Brāhman. <i>—Brahmāraṇya</i> <i>(°ma-ar°), am,</i> n. ‘forest of religious knowledge,’ a grove in which the Vedas are read and explained; N. of a forest. <i>—Brahmārambha (°ma-ār°), as,</i> m. beginning to repeat the Veda (Manu II. 71). <i>—Brahmārgha (°ma-ar°), as, ā, am,</i> Ved. worthy of sacred knowledge; worthy of Brahma; (in the Kauṣītaki Upaniṣad I. 1, a various reading for <i>brahma-grāhin,</i> q. v.) <i>—Brahmārpaṇa (°ma-</i> <i>ar°), am,</i> n. the offering or oblation of sacred knowledge; N. of a magical spell (see <i>manu</i>). <i>—Brahmālaṅkāra (°ma-al°), as,</i> m., Ved. the ornament of Brahmā, (according to a Scholiast <i>=</i> <i>hiraṇyagarbha-yogyam maṇḍanam.</i>) <i>—Brah-</i> <i>māvarta (°ma-āv°), as,</i> m. ‘the holy land,’ an epithet of the country situated between the rivers Sarasvatī and Dṛṣadvatī to the N. W. of Hastināpura (Manu II. 17); N. of a Tīrtha; N. of one of the sons of Ṛṣabha. <i>—Brahmāvarta-tīrtha, am,</i> n., N. of a Tīrtha on the Revā or Narmadā river. <i>—Brahmāvāsa (°ma-āv°), as,</i> m., N. of a Vedānta philosophical work; (also called Avimukta-nirukti.) <i>—Brahmāsana (°ma-ās°), am,</i> n. the seat of the Brahman priest (Ved.); a particular posture suited to devout religious meditation. <i>—Brahmāsana-niviṣṭa,</i> <i>as, ā, am,</i> seated in the posture called Brahmāsana. <i>—Brahmāstra (°ma-as°), am,</i> n. ‘Brahmā's missile,’ N. of a fabled weapon (supposed to be the gift of Brahmā) which deals infallible destruction; ‘the imprecation of a Brāhman,’ a term applied to a particular kind of incantation. <i>—Brahmāsya (°ma-</i> <i>ās°), am,</i> n. the mouth of a Brāhman. <i>—Brahmā-</i> <i>huta (°ma-āh°), as, ā, am,</i> Ved. one to whom oblations of prayer or devotion have been made. <i>—Brahmāhuti (°ma-āh°), is,</i> f. the offering of prayer or devotion; [cf. <i>brahma-yajña, brahma-sattra.</i>] <i>—Brahmeddha (°ma-id°), as, ā, am,</i> Ved. lighted or kindled during prayer. <i>—Brahme-śaya</i> (<i>brahme</i> for <i>brahmaṇi</i>), <i>as,</i> m. ‘reposing or resting in Brahman,’ an epithet of Kārttikeya; of Viṣṇu. <i>—Brahmeśvara-tīrtha (°ma-īś°), am,</i> n., N. of a Tīrtha on the Revā or Narmadā river. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>mojjhatā (°ma-uj°),</i> f. neglecting or forgetting the Vedas, (according to Kullūka on Manu XI. 56 <i>= adhīta-vedasyānabhyāsena vismaraṇam.</i>) <i>—Brahmoḍumbara,</i> another form for <i>brahmo-</i> <i>dumbara,</i> q. v. <i>—Brahmottara (°ma-ut°), as, ā,</i> <i>am,</i> treating particularly of Brahman [cf. <i>bṛhad-</i> <i>brahmottara-khaṇḍa</i>]; consisting chiefly of Brāhmans; (<i>as</i>), m., N. of a superhuman being; (<i>ās</i>), m. pl. ‘mostly Brāhmans,’ N. of a people; (<i>am</i>), n., N. of a section of the Skanda-Purāṇa. <i>—Brah-</i> <i>mottara-khaṇḍa, am,</i> n., N. of a section of the Skanda-Purāṇa. <i>—Brahmottara-purāṇa, am,</i> n., N. of a supplementary section of the Brahma-Purāṇa. <i>—Brahmoda-tīrtha (°ma-ud°), am,</i> n., N. of a Tīrtha mentioned in the Śiva-Purāṇa. <i>—Brahmo-</i> <i>dumbara (°ma-ud°),</i> N. of a place of pilgrimage. <i>—Brahmodya (°ma-ud°), am,</i> n. rivalry in sacred knowledge, playful discussion of theological problems or enigmas, reciting or explaining the Veda, speaking or treating of religious knowledge. <i>—Brahmopa-</i> <i>deśa (°ma-up°), as,</i> m. instruction in divine knowledge. <i>—Brahmopaniṣad (°ma-up°), t,</i> f. mystical teaching concerning Brahma (Ved.); a mystical Brāhmanical treatise; N. of an Upaniṣad mentioned in the Tantra-sāra; of an Upaniṣad belonging to the Atharva-veda. <i>—Brahmaudana (°ma-od°),</i> <i>as,</i> m., Ved. boiled rice distributed to Brāhmans and especially to priests at a sacrifice. <i>—Brahmau-</i> <i>pagava (°ma-aup°),</i> see Scholiast on Pāṇ. VI. 1, 88."

The superintending or presiding priest at the sacrifice. 4. One of the astronomical Yogas. 5. One of the principal servants of the Jinas. n. (-ह्म) 1. The divine cause and essence of the world, from which all created things are supposed to emanate and to which they return; the unknown God. 2. The practice of austere devotion. 3. The Vedas or scripture. 4. Holy knowledge. E. वृह् to increase, (mankind) aff. मनिन् and the initial letter changed to ब ।"

            "content": "1. <b>Brahman</b>¦ (neut.) denotes the priestly class as opposed to the warrior class and the people (<b>Kṣatra</b> and <b>Viś</b>). The term is found in the Atharvaveda,<sup>1</sup> and repeatedly later on.<sup>2</sup> For the position, etc., of this class, see <b>Brāhmaṇa.</b> <F>1) ii. 15, 4; ix. 7, 9; xii. 5, 8; xv. 10, 3, 4.</F> <F>2) Taittirīya Saṃhitā, iii. 3, 1, 1, etc.; Vājasaneyi Saṃhitā, vi. 3; vii. 21, etc. See also <b>Varṇa</b> and <b>Kṣatra.</b></F>"

            "content": "2. <b>Brahman</b>¦ is found in many passages of the Rigveda and later in the sense of ‘priest.’ In many passages of the Rigveda<sup>1</sup> he is referred to as praising the gods; in others<sup>2</sup> the sense of ‘priest’ is adequate. In not a few cases<sup>3</sup> the priesthood as a profession is clearly alluded to, nor is there any reason to doubt<sup>4</sup> that in all cases the word has the technical sense of a member of the priesthood. There is, however, considerable doubt as to the number of cases in the Rigveda, where it has the technical sense of the priest who guides the sacrifice generally. It is undoubtedly found in that sense, both Muir<sup>5</sup> and Roth<sup>6</sup> recognizing instances of its being used thus. Geldner,<sup>7</sup> however, is anxious to find that sense in a large number of passages, and insists that the <b>Purohita</b> was normally a Brahman in the narrower sense. Oldenberg,<sup>8</sup> on the other hand, holds with greater probability that in most of the passages adduced Brahman means simply ‘priest,’ and that the Purohita, who was essentially not a member of the ordinary body of sacrificing priests (<b>Ṛtvij</b>), was, when he officiated at the sacrifice, more usually the Hotṛ priest, and only later became the Brahman. This change he regards as having taken place when the importance of the hymns declined, and most weight was laid on the functions of the priest who superintended the sacrifice as a whole, and by his magic repaired the flaws in the sacrifice.<sup>9</sup> In the later literature both senses of the word are quite common.<sup>10</sup> <F>1) i. 80, 1; 164, 34; ii. 2, 6; vi. 45, 7; vii. 33, 11; viii. 16, 7; x. 71, 11; 77, 1; 85, 3, 16. 34; 107, 6; 117, 7; 125, 5; Muir, <i>Sanskrit Texts,</i> 12, 244-246.</F> <F>2) i. 10, 1; 33, 9; 101, 5; 108, 7; 158, 6; ii. 39, 1; iv. 50, 8, 9; 58, 2; v. 29, 3; 31, 4; 32, 12; 40, 8; vii. 7, 5; 42, 1; viii. 7, 20; 17, 2; 31, 1; 32, 16; 33 19; 45, 39; 64, 7; 77, 5; 92, 30; 96, 5; ix. 96, 6; 112, 1; 113, 6; x. 28 11; 71, 11; 85, 29; 141, 3; Muir, <i>op. cit.,</i> 12, 246-251.</F> <F>3) i. 108, 7; iv. 50, 8, 9; viii. 7, 20; 45, 39; 64, 7; 92, 30; ix. 112, 1; x. 85, 29; Muir, 12, 258.</F> <F>4) <i>Loc. cit. Cf.</i> Zimmer, <i>Altindisches</i> <i>Leben,</i> 190 <i>et seq.</i></F> <F>5) <i>Op. cit.,</i> 12, 251, citing ii. 1, 2 (= ix. 91, 10); iv. 9, 4; x. 52, 2.</F> <F>6) St. Petersburg Dictionary, <i>s.v.</i> 2, citing ii. 1, 2; ix. 96, 6; x. 71, 11; 107, 6. In none of the last three passages is the specific sense cogently required.</F> <F>7) <i>Vedische Studien,</i> 2, 145 <i>et seq.;</i> 3, 155. He thinks that the sense of ‘superintending priest’ is the older, and sees it in i. 158, 6; iv. 9, 4; 50, 7. 8; vii. 7, 5; 33, 11; x. 141, 3, etc.</F> <F>8) <i>Religion des Veda,</i> 396, 397, who thinks that the Brahman priest known to the Rigveda was the <b>Brāhmaṇāc-</b> <b>chaṃsin</b> and who in most passages (<i>e.g.,</i> iv. 50, 7. 8) sees only the sense of ‘priest.’ <i>Cf.</i> Weber, <i>Indische Studien,</i> 10, 376, 377.</F> <F>9) <i>Cf.</i> Pischel, <i>Göttingische Gelehrte</i> <i>Anzeigen,</i> 1894, 420; Hillebrandt, <i>Ritual-</i> <i>litteratur,</i> 13; Bloomfield, <i>Hymns of the</i> <i>Atharvaveda,</i> lxviii; <i>Atharvaveda,</i> 32; and see <b>Purohita.</b></F> <F>10) As ‘priest,’ Av. ii. 7, 2; iv. 35, 1. 2; v. 8, 5; 17, 8; 18, 7; 19, 8; vi. 122, 5; viii. 9, 3; x. 1, 3; 4, 30. 33; 7, 24; xi. 1, 25; xii. 1, 38; xix. 32, 8; Taittirīya Saṃhitā, iv. 1, 7, 1; Vājasaneyi Saṃhitā, xxvi. 2; Aitareya Brāhmaṇa, v. 3, etc. As ‘superintending priest,’ Av. xviii. 4, 15; xx. 2, 3; Taittirīya Saṃhitā, i. 8, 9, 1; ii. 3, 11, 4; iii. 5, 2, 1, etc.; Kāṭhaka Saṃhitā, xxxvii. 17; and see Weber, <i>Indische</i> <i>Studien,</i> 10, 34, 35; 114; 135-138; 327; 330-337.</F>"

<q>यल्लाभान्नापरो लाभो यत्सुखान्नापरं सुखम् । यज्ज्ञानान्नापरं ज्ञानं तद्ब्रह्मेत्यवधारयेत् । यद् दृष्ट्वा नापरं दृश्यं यद्भुत्वा न पुनर्भवः । यज्ज्ञात्वा नापरं ज्ञेयं तद्ब्रह्मेत्यबधारयेत् । तिर्य्यगूर्द्धमधः पूर्णं सचिदानन्दमद्वयम् । अनन्तं नित्यमेकं यत्तदिब्रह्मे­त्यबधारयेत् । अतद्व्यावृत्तिरूपेण वैदान्तैर्लक्ष्यतेऽद्वयम् । अखण्डानन्दमेकं यत् तद्ब्रह्मेन्यवधारयेत् । दृश्यते श्रूयते यद्यद्ब्रह्मणोऽन्यन्न तद्भवेत् । तत्त्वज्ञानाच्च तद्ब्रह्म सच्चि­दानन्दमद्वयम् । सर्वगं सच्चिदात्मानं ज्ञानचक्षुर्निरीक्षते । अज्ञानचक्षुर्नेक्षेत भास्वन्तं भानुमन्धवत्</q> । तच्च निर्गुण­मपि गुणभेदेन नानारूपं यथोक्तम् <q>ब्रह्मैकं मूर्त्तिभेदस्तु गुणभेदेन सन्ततम् । तद्ब्रह्म द्विविधं बस्तु सगुणं निर्गुणं शिव! । मायाश्रितो यः सगुणो माया­तीतञ्च निर्गुणः । स्वेच्छामयश्च भगवानिच्छया विकरोति च । इच्छाशक्तिश्च प्रकृतिः सर्वशक्ति­प्रसूः सदा । केचिदेकं वदन्त्येवं ब्रह्म ज्योतिः सनातनम् । केचिद्वदन्ति द्विविधं ब्रह्मप्रकृतिपू­र्वकम् । शृणु ये च वदन्त्येकं प्रकृतिपुरुषयोः परम् । तस्माद्भवति तौ द्वौ च तद्ब्रह्म सर्वकारणम्</q> । अथवैकं परं ब्रह्म द्विविधं भवतीच्छया । इच्छाशक्तिश्च प्रकृतिः सर्वशक्तिप्रसूः सदा” ब्रह्मवैवर्त्ते जन्मख° ४३ अ° । तस्य नवधा रूपं यथा <q>योगिनो यं वदन्त्येवं ज्योतीरूपं सनातनम् १ । जयोतिरभ्यन्तरे नित्य रूपं २ भक्ता वदन्ति यम् । वेदा वदन्ति सत्यं ३ यं नित्यमाद्यं ४ विचक्षणाः । यं वदन्ति सुराः सर्वे परं स्वेच्छामयं प्रभुम् ५ । सिद्धेन्द्रास्य्नयः सर्वे
